Exception of Non-Measurable Items from Dirham Debt
Ruling on exception of non-measurable items from dirham debt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exception of a non-measurable item from a dirham debt and identify the condition of genus unity.

Core Idea
Exception of a non-measurable item from a dirham debt is void; the full debt remains due.

This lesson presents a clear rule from the Hanafi school regarding exceptions (istithna) in acknowledgments. When the exception involves an item of a different genus than the debt, the exception is invalid, and the full amount is owed. The key condition is 'ittihad jinsi' (genus unity). We will examine the ruling, its basis, and the contrasting view of Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is an exception (istithna) of a non-measurable item from a debt of dirhams. The Hanafi ruling is that the exception is void (batil).
2
Locate the condition
The ruling hinges on the condition of genus unity (ittihad jinsi): the excepted item must belong to the same genus as the debt. Dirhams are weighable (wazni), so only weighable or measurable (kayli) items of the same genus can be excepted.
Non-measurable items like cloth, house, or sheep are not of the same genus as dirhams.
3
Apply to the examples
The passage gives examples: cloth, house, sheep. None are weighable or measurable like dirhams, so the exception fails in each case.
The exception is void by agreement of the Hanafi school (bi-ittifaq as-habuna).
4
Note the consequence
Since the exception is void, the full original debt (e.g., 100 dirhams) remains binding on the debtor.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the value of the excepted item is deducted from the debt. For Hanafis, value deduction is irrelevant without genus unity.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf between the schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن استثنى غير الكيلي والوزني من الدراهم لم يصح الاستثناء باتفاق أصحابنا ، فإذا قال : له علي مئة درهم إلا ثوباً أو داراً أو شاة بطل الاستثناء اتفاقاً، ويلزمه مئة درهم ؛ لأن ذلك القدر لا يفيد الاتحاد الجنسي، وعند الشافعي له يطرح قيمته من المستثنى منه .
And if he excepts something other than measurable or weighable from dirhams, the exception is not valid by the agreement of our companions. So if he says: 'I owe him one hundred dirhams except a cloth, or a house, or a sheep,' the exception is void by agreement, and one hundred dirhams are binding upon him, because that amount does not effect genus unity. And with al-Shafi'i, its value is deducted from the excepted-from amount.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage states a clear ruling from the Hanafi school: Exception of an item that is not of the same genus as the debt (here, dirhams, which are weighable) is invalid. The examples given are cloth, house, and sheep – none of which are measured by weight or volume like dirhams. Therefore, the exception is void, and the full debt remains due. The text notes that this is agreed upon by all Hanafi authorities (as-habuna). In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the value of the excepted item is subtracted from the debt, a view already addressed in the previous lesson. The rationale for the Hanafi ruling is that such an exception does not achieve 'jinsi ittihad' (genus unity), meaning the excepted item cannot be considered a part of the acknowledged genus.

Key Terms
كيلي (kayli): Items measured by volume (like grains).
وزني (wazni): Items measured by weight (like dirhams, gold).
اتحاد جنسي (ittihad jinsi): Unity of genus; the condition that the excepted item belongs to the same genus as the acknowledged debt for a valid exception.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone says 'I owe you 100 dirhams except this sheep,' according to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling?
A) The exception is valid and the value of the sheep is deducted.
B) The exception is void and 100 dirhams are due.
C) The acknowledgement is void.
D) Only the sheep is given to the creditor.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, exception of a non-genus item from a debt is void due to lack of genus unity (ittihad jinsi).

Void Acknowledgement: The Effect of 'In Sha Allah'
Ruling on acknowledgement conditioned on Allah's will

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that an acknowledgement conditioned on Allah's will is void and distinguish it from a conditional specification of a term.

Core Idea
Conditioning an acknowledgement voids it because it is a report, not a creative act.

In legal practice, an acknowledgement (iqrar) is a report of a right. The Hanafi school strictly holds that such a report cannot be suspended on a future condition. This lesson examines the ruling when a person says 'in sha Allah' while acknowledging a debt, and why it entirely nullifies the acknowledgement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is an acknowledgement (iqrar) of a debt accompanied by the phrase 'in sha Allah'. According to the Hanafi school, this renders the acknowledgement void (batil) and no obligation arises.
The ruling applies to any condition that suspends the acknowledgement on a future event, not just 'in sha Allah'.
2
Understand the two Hanafi interpretations
Abu Yusuf considered the phrase an annulment (ibtaal) of the ruling before it takes effect. Muhammad al-Shaybani considered it an invalid condition (ta'liq batil) because an acknowledgement is a report (khabar) and reports cannot be conditional.
Both interpretations lead to the same conclusion: the acknowledgement is void.
3
Distinguish between ta'liq and tawqit
Not all conditional language voids the acknowledgement. If the condition specifies a term (ajal), such as 'if I die' or 'at the beginning of the month', it is considered a valid deferment, not a condition. This is because custom treats such phrases as specifying when the debt is due.
If the creditor denies the term, the debt becomes immediately due because the term is not agreed upon.
4
Apply the distinction to other phrases
Phrases like 'if Allah decrees', 'if it rains', etc., that do not specify a term void the acknowledgement. But phrases that customarily indicate a due date are valid deferments.
The key is whether the phrase is understood as a condition on the existence of the debt or a specification of its time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَطَلَ إقراره. ولو استثنى بناء دارٍ أقر بها ، كانا للمُقرِ له)؛ لأنَّ الأستثناء لا يصح؛ لأن البناء إنما يدخلُ بالتبعية، وما هو كذلك لا يصح استثناؤه بإقراره، بأن قال : لفلان علي مئة درهم إن شاء الله تعالى بطل إقراره ، ولا يلزمُهُ ما أقر به، فإنَّ الاستثناء بمشيئة الله تعالى إبطال للحكم قبل انعقاده، وبه قال أبو يوسف، أو تعليق بشرط لا يوقف عليه، وبه قال محمد. كما صرح به قاضي خان في «شرح الجامع الصغير». وروي الخلاف على العكس، وعلى كلا القولين أبطل الإقرار، أما على كونه إيطالاً فظاهر وأما على كونه تعليقاً بالشرط؛ فلأن الإقرار لا يحتمل التعليق بالشرط؛ لأن الإقرار إخبار، والإخبار لا يحتمله، فإنّه إن كان صدقاً لا يصير كذباً؛ لفوات الشرط، وإن كان كذباً لا يصير صدقاً؛ لوجود الشرط، وإنما يليق بالإيجاب ليتبين بالتعليق أنه ليس بإيقاع ما لم يوجد الشرط. [١] قوله : بطل إقراره؛ وكذا كل إقرار عُلّق بالشرط، مثل أن يقول : إن دخلت الدار أو مطرت السماء، أو هبت الريح، أو إن قضى الله تعالى، أو أراده، أو رضيه، أو أحبه، أو قدره، أو يسرَه ، فهذا كلّه وما شاكله مبطلاً للإقرار إذا كان موصولاً صرح به الزَّيْلَعِيُّ في «شرح الكنز»). بخلاف ما إذا قال لفلان علي مئة درهم إذا مت أو إذا جاءَ رأس الشهر أو إذا أفطر الناس؛ لأنه في معنى بيان المدّة من حيث العرف؛ لأنّ هذه الأشياء تذكر في العادة لبيان محل الأجل، فاعتبر إقراراً بدين مؤجل فيكون تأجيلاً، لا تعليقاً بالشرط، حتى لو كذبه المقر له في الأجل يكون المال حالاً. كما هو المصرح في «الهداية»(۲)، وغيرها.
His acknowledgement is void. And if he excepts the building of a house he acknowledged, then both are for the acknowledgee, because the exception is not valid; because the building enters by implication, and what is like that, its exception is not valid in his acknowledgement. For if he says: 'I owe so-and-so one hundred dirhams if Allah wills,' his acknowledgement is void, and what he acknowledged is not binding upon him. Because exception by the will of Allah Almighty is an annulment of the ruling before its conclusion, and this is the view of Abu Yusuf. Or it is a condition upon which nothing depends, and this is the view of Muhammad, as stated by Qadi Khan in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir. It is reported that the difference is reversed. On both opinions, the acknowledgement is void. As for it being an annulment, it is apparent. As for it being a conditional, because acknowledgement does not admit of conditionality, because acknowledgement is a report, and a report does not admit it. Because if it is true, it does not become false due to the non-occurrence of the condition, and if it is false, it does not become true due to the occurrence of the condition. Conditionality is only appropriate for creation (insha') to clarify that it is not a conclusion until the condition is met. [1] His words: 'His acknowledgement is void' – and likewise every acknowledgement conditioned upon a condition, such as if he says: 'If the house enters, or the sky rains, or the wind blows, or if Allah decrees, or wills, or approves, or loves, or determines, or facilitates' – all this and similar voids the acknowledgement if it is connected, as stated by al-Zayla'i in Sharh al-Kanz. Unlike if he says: 'I owe so-and-so one hundred dirhams if I die, or if the beginning of the month comes, or if the people break their fast' – because this is in the sense of specifying a term customarily, because these things are usually mentioned to specify the term, so it is considered an acknowledgement of a deferred debt, thus it is a deferment, not a condition. So if the acknowledgee denies the term, the money is due immediately, as stated in al-Hidayah and others.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when someone makes an acknowledgement and connects it with 'in sha Allah' (if Allah wills). The Hanafi school rules that such an acknowledgement is void and the debtor is not liable. The text presents two interpretations from the early Hanafi masters: Abu Yusuf views the phrase as an annulment (ibtaal) of the ruling before its establishment, while Muhammad al-Shaybani sees it as a conditional suspension (ta'liq) that is invalid because an acknowledgement is a report (khabar), which cannot be suspended on a condition. Al-Qadi Khan notes that the reported difference might be reversed, but on both views the acknowledgement is void. The reason is that a report is either true or false regardless of conditions; adding a condition does not change its truth value. In contrast, conditional language is only suitable for creative statements (insha'), such as contracts. The passage then clarifies that other conditional expressions like 'if I die' or 'if the month begins' are not considered conditions but rather specifications of the term (ajal), making the debt deferred, not conditional. If the creditor denies the deferment, the debt becomes immediately due due to disagreement on the term.

Key Terms
إن شاء الله (in sha Allah): A phrase meaning 'if Allah wills,' used here as a condition in an acknowledgement.
إقرار (iqrar): An acknowledgement of a right; considered a report (khabar), not a creative act (insha').
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspension of a ruling upon a future condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person says 'I owe you 100 dirhams if Allah wills,' what is the ruling?
A) The debt is valid but deferred until Allah wills.
B) The acknowledgement is void and no debt is owed.
C) The debt is valid but the condition is ignored.
D) The acknowledgement is valid as a conditional debt.

Key Takeaway
Conditioning an acknowledgement on 'in sha Allah' voids it entirely because iqrar is a report and cannot be conditional.

Conditional Iqrar: Why 'In Sha' Allah' Voids a Confession in Hanafi Law
Ruling on conditional iqrar with 'in sha' Allah' and similar phrases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional iqrar, explain the distinction between ta'liq and ta'jil, and apply the ruling to scenarios involving 'in sha' Allah' versus time-based phrases.

Core Idea
A confession conditional on a future uncertain event is void because iqrar is declarative, not performative.

In Hanafi law, making a confession (iqrar) is a serious legal act. But what happens if the confessor adds 'if Allah wills' (in sha' Allah)? This lesson unpacks the ruling from the Hanafi tradition, explaining why such a condition voids the confession and how the school distinguishes between true conditional suspension (ta'liq) and mere deferral (ta'jil).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is an iqrar (confession) that includes a conditional phrase like 'in sha' Allah'. The ruling from the text is that such an iqrar is batil (void).
This is the starting point: the confession does not bind the confessor.
2
Understand the legal nature of iqrar
Iqrar is classified as ikhbar (a declarative statement) in Hanafi usul. Unlike insha' (performatives like contracts or oaths), ikhbar does not admit ta'liq (suspension) because its truth value is determined at the time of utterance.
This is the key usul principle underlying the ruling.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi explanation
Abu Yusuf views the phrase 'in sha' Allah' as an annulment (ibtal) before the ruling takes effect; Muhammad views it as a conditional suspension (ta'liq) that iqrar cannot bear. Both agree the iqrar is void.
The difference is theoretical; the practical outcome is the same.
4
Distinguish valid deferral (ta'jil) from invalid suspension
Phrases like 'when I die' or 'at the start of the month' are interpreted as specifying the term of payment (ta'jil) based on custom. They are not true conditions; the iqrar is valid as a deferred debt.
This distinction prevents over-application of the rule.
5
Apply the ruling to new examples
Test other phrases from the text (e.g., 'if it rains', 'if Allah decrees') as void, and distinguish phrases that indicate a definite term (ta'jil).
Practice with the scenarios in the practice tasks.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَطَلَ إقراره". ولو استثنى بناء دارٍ أقر بها ، كانا للمُقرِ له)؛ لأنَّ الأستثناء لا يصح؛ لأن البناء إنما يدخلُ بالتبعية، وما هو كذلك لا يصح استثناؤه. بإقراره، بأن قال : لفلان علي مئة درهم إن شاء الله تعالى بطل إقراره ، ولا يلزمة ما أقر به، فإنَّ الاستثناء بمشيئة الله تعالى إبطال للحكم قبل انعقاده، وبه قال أبو يوسف، أو تعليق بشرط لا يوقف عليه، وبه قال محمد . كما صرح به قاضي خان في «شرح الجامع الصغير». وروي الخلاف على العكس، وعلى كلا القولين أبطل الإقرار، أما على كونه إيطالاً فظاهر وأما على كونه تعليقاً بالشرط؛ فلأن الإقرار لا يحتمل التعليق بالشرط؛ لأن الإقرار إخبار، والإخبار لا يحتمله، فإنّه إن كان صدقاً لا يصير كذباً؛ لفوات الشرط، وإن كان كذباً لا يصير صدقاً؛ لوجود الشرط، وإنما يليق بالإيجاب ليتبين بالتعليق أنه ليس بإيقاع ما لم يوجد الشرط. [١] قوله : بطل إقراره؛ وكذا كل إقرار عُلّق بالشرط، مثل أن يقول : إن دخلت الدار أو مطرت السماء، أو هبت الريح، أو إن قضى الله تعالى، أو أراده، أو رضيه، أو أحبه، أو قدره، أو يسرَه، فهذا كلّه وما شاكله مبطلاً للإقرار إذا كان موصولاً صرح به الزَّيْلَعِيُّ في «شرح الكنز»). بخلاف ما إذا قال لفلان علي مئة درهم إذا مت أو إذا جاءَ رأس الشهر أو إذا أفطر الناس؛ لأنه في معنى بيان المدة من حيث العرف؛ لأن هذه الأشياء تذكر في العادة لبيان محل الأجل، فاعتبر إقراراً بدين مؤجل فيكون تأجيلاً، لا تعليقاً بالشرط، حتى لو كذبه المقر له في الأجل يكون المال حالاً. كما هو المصرح في «الهداية»، وغيرها.
His confession is void. And if he made an exception of the building of a house which he confessed [to owning], both are for the confesse. Because the exception is invalid; for the building enters only as a dependent, and what is like that, its exception is not valid. By his confession — if he said: 'I owe so-and-so one hundred dirhams, if Allah wills', his confession is void, and he is not obligated by what he confessed. Indeed, the exception by 'if Allah wills' is an annulment of the ruling before its occurrence (as per Abu Yusuf), or a suspension upon a condition which is not uncovered (as per Muhammad). As Qadi Khan stated in his commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir. And it is narrated that the disagreement [between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] is reversed. In both opinions, the confession is void. As for it being an annulment, it is apparent; as for it being a suspension by a condition, it is because confession does not admit of suspension by a condition, because confession is news, and news does not admit it. For if it is true, it does not become false due to the failure of the condition; and if it is false, it does not become true due to the occurrence of the condition. It is only befitting to an oath to make clear by the suspension that there is no effectuation until the condition occurs. [1] His statement: 'His confession is void.' Likewise, every confession suspended on a condition, such that he says: 'if you enter the house, or if it rains, or if the wind blows, or if Allah decrees it, or wills it, or is pleased with it, or loves it, or predestines it, or facilitates it' — all this and what resembles it invalidates the confession if it is connected. As stated by al-Zayla'i in Sharh al-Kanz. Unlike if he said: 'I owe so-and-so one hundred dirhams when I die, or when the new month comes, or when people break fast' — because it is in the meaning of specifying the term from a customary perspective, for these things are usually mentioned to specify the due date, so it is considered a confession of a deferred debt, thus it is deferral, not a conditional suspension. So much so that if the confesse denies the term, the money is due immediately. As is explicitly stated in al-Hidayah and others.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah deals with the validity of conditional confessions (iqrar) in Hanafi law. It opens with a ruling: if someone makes a confession (e.g., owing money) and adds 'if Allah wills' (in sha' Allah), the confession is void (batil). The commentator explains the reasoning: the phrase 'in sha' Allah' is either an annulment of the ruling before it takes effect (according to Abu Yusuf) or a suspension on a condition that cannot be verified (according to Muhammad). Despite the difference in analysis, both agree the iqrar is void. The passage then provides a general rule: any iqrar suspended on a condition (like entering a house, rain, wind, or any divine attribute) is invalid, provided the condition is attached immediately (mawsul). However, an important distinction is made: if the condition relates to a future event that customarily indicates a deferral (ta'jil) of payment, such as 'when I die' or 'when the month begins,' it is considered a valid iqrar for a deferred debt, not a conditional suspension. This is because such phrases are understood in common usage as specifying the term of payment rather than suspending the obligation itself. The practical consequence: if the confesse disputes the term, the debt becomes due immediately.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): A legal confession or acknowledgment of a right or debt.
استثناء بمشيئة الله (istithna' bi mashyi'at Allah): The phrase 'in sha' Allah' attached to a confession, which invalidates it.
تعليق بالشرط (ta'liq bi al-shart): Suspending the effect of a statement on the occurrence of a future condition.
إخبار (ikhbar): A declarative statement that informs about a past or present fact.
تأجيل (ta'jil): Specifying a due date for a deferred debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is an iqrar (confession) conditional upon 'if Allah wills' (in sha' Allah) considered void in the Hanafi school?
A) Because it contradicts the Quranic command to fulfill promises.
B) Because iqrar is an ikhbar (declarative statement) that cannot be suspended on a condition.
C) Because the condition is impossible to verify.
D) Because the phrase 'in sha' Allah' is only permissible in oaths.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a confession (iqrar) conditional upon an uncertain future event is void because iqrar is declarative (ikhbar) and cannot be suspended; however, conditions that customarily indicate a payment term are valid as deferral (ta'jil).

Exception of the Building in Iqrar: Invalid
Ruling on exception of building in iqrar of a house.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that the building is included in iqrar of a house by dependency (taba'iyya) and explain that verbal exception of the building is invalid, while exception of a part (e.g., a room) is valid.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, the building is a dependent description in a house; therefore, excepting it in an iqrar is void, but excepting a part is valid.

This lesson examines a key ruling in Hanafi iqrar (confession) law: when someone confesses to owning a house, the building is automatically included. Any attempt to verbally exclude the building from the confession is legally ineffective. The commentary explains the linguistic and juristic basis, distinguishing between a dependent description and an integral part.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
A person confesses 'this house is for Zayd' but adds 'except the building'. The ruling: both the house and building go to Zayd; the exception is invalid.
The exception is a verbal attempt to exclude.
2
Understand the linguistic basis
The word 'dar' (house) in Arabic primarily denotes the open ground (arsa); the building is a description (wasf) that enters by dependency (taba'iyya).
The building is not a direct part of the name.
3
Apply the principle of taba'iyya
Since the building is a dependent, it is included automatically. Exception (istithna') operates only on what is directly included; dependents cannot be excepted.
4
Contrast with exception of a part
If the exception is of a third or a specific room, it is valid because these are integral parts of the house directly under the word 'dar'.
Parts are directly included; descriptions are not.
5
Conclude the practical effect
The confesse (Zayd) gets the entire property. The confessor's attempt to retain the building fails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو استثنى بناء دار أقر بها، كانا للمقر له؛ لأن الأستثناء لا يصح؛ لأن البناء إنما يدخل بالتبعية، وما هو كذلك لا يصح استثناؤه. [٢] قوله : ولو استثنى...الخ؛ يعني لو أقر بدار واستثنى بناءها لنفسه، بأن قال : هذه الدار لزيد، وبناؤها لنفسي، كان الدار والبناء جميعاً للمقر له؛ لأن البناء دخل في لفظ الإقرار بالدار تبعاً لا مقصوداً، فإن اسم الدار لا يتناول البناء مقصوداً؛ لأن الدار اسم للعرصة، والبناء وصف فيه، والوصف يدخل تبعاً لا قصداً، والاستثناء تصرف لفظي فما يتناوله اسم الدار لا يتحقق فيه عمل الاستثناء، فلا يصح. بخلاف ما إذا قال: إلا ثلثها، أو إلا بيتاً منها، حيث يصح الاستثناء، ويكون للمقر له ما عدا ثلث الدار، وما عدا البيت؛ لأن أجزاء الدار داخلة تحت لفظ الدار فصح استثناؤها، حتى لو استحق هذا الجزء في بيع الدار يسقط حصته من الثمن. وقوله : وعرصتها لك؛ عرصه الدار: ساحتها، وهي البقعة الواسعة التي ليس فيها بناء، والجمع عراص، مثل: كلبة وكِلاب، وعَرصات، مثل سجدة وسجدات. وقال أبو المنصور التَّعَالِبي: كل بقعة ليس فيها بناء فهي عرصة، وفي كلام ابن فارس له نحو ذلك، وفي التهذيب: سُمِّيت ساحة الدار عرصة؛ لأن الصبيان يعترصون فيها؛ أي يلعبون ويمرحون. كذا في «المصباح المنير». وقوله : فكما قال؛ يعني يكون البناء للمقر، والعرصة للمقر له؛ لأن العرصة عبارة عن البقعة دون البناء، فصار كأنه قال: بياضُ هذا الدار دون البناء لفلان، بخلاف ما إذا قال: مكان العرصة الأرض، بأن قال: بناء هذه الدار لي وأرضها لفلان، حيث يكون له البناء أيضاً؛ لأن الأرض كالدار فيتبعها البناء. بخلاف ما إذا قال بناء هذه الدار لزيد والأرض لعمرو، حيث يكون لكل واحد منهما ما أقر به له؛ لأنه لما أقر بالبناء لزيدٍ صار ملكاً له فلا يخرج من ملكه بإقراره لعمرو بالأرض، إذ لا يصدق قوله في حق غيره، بخلاف المسألة الأولى؛ لأن البناء مملولاً له، فإذا أقرّ بالأرض لغيره يتبعها؛ لأن إقراره مقبول في حق نفسه. ولو قال : أرض هذه الدار لفلان وبناؤها لي أو لفلان، كان الكل للأول؛ لأنه لما أقر بالأرض له ملك البناء تبعاً، فلا يقبل قوله بعد ذلك أنه لغيره، ولو قال : بناء هذه الدار لفلان وأرضها لفلان فلكل واحدٍ منهما ما أقر له به؛ لقيام ملكه عند الإقرار.
And if he made an exception of the building of a house which he confessed [to owning], both are for the confesse; because the exception is invalid; for the building enters only as a dependent, and what is like that, its exception is not valid. [2] His statement: 'And if he excepted...' means: if he confessed to a house and excepted its building for himself, saying: 'This house is for Zayd, and its building for myself,' both the house and the building are for the confesse; because the building entered the wording of the confession of the house as a dependent, not as an intended object. Indeed, the name 'house' does not comprehend the building as an intended object; because 'house' is a name for the open ground (arsa), and the building is a description in it, and the description enters dependently, not intentionally. Exception is a verbal operation, and what the name 'house' covers, the operation of exception is not realized in it, so it is invalid. Unlike if he said: 'except a third of it,' or 'except a room of it,' where the exception is valid, and the confesse gets what is other than a third of the house and other than the room; because the parts of the house are included under the word 'house,' so their exception is valid. So much so that if this part is claimed in the sale of the house, its portion of the price is dropped. And his statement: 'and its open ground (arsa) is for you.' 'Arsat al-dar' means its courtyard, the wide space that has no building. The plural is 'aras' like 'kalba' and 'kilab', and 'arasat' like 'sajda' and 'sajadat'. Abu al-Mansur al-Tha'alibi said: every space that has no building is an 'arsa'. In the words of Ibn Faris there is something similar. And in al-Tahdhib: the courtyard of a house is called 'arsa' because children play (ya'tarisun) there. As in al-Misbah al-Munir. And his statement: 'it is as he said' means: the building is for the confessor and the open ground is for the confesse; because 'arsa' means the space without building, so it is as if he said: 'the empty part of this house without the building is for so-and-so.' Unlike if he used the word 'earth' instead of 'arsa', saying: 'the building of this house is for me and its earth for so-and-so,' where the building is also for him (the confessor); because the earth is like the house, so the building follows it. Unlike if he said: 'the building of this house is for Zayd and the earth for Amr,' where each gets what he confessed to him; because when he confessed the building to Zayd, it became his property, so it does not leave his ownership by his confession of the earth to Amr, since his statement is not credible against others. This is different from the first issue; because the building is his property, so when he confesses the earth to someone else, it (the building) follows it; because his confession is accepted regarding himself. And if he said: 'the earth of this house is for so-and-so and its building for me or for so-and-so,' then all is for the first [mentioned]; because when he confessed the earth to him, the building becomes his as a dependent, so his subsequent statement that it is for someone else is not accepted. And if he said: 'the building of this house is for so-and-so and its earth for so-and-so,' then each gets what he confessed to him; because of the establishment of his ownership at the time of confession.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on al-Wiqayah's chapter on iqrar (confession), specifically addressing the ruling on excepting (istithna') the building (bina') when confessing to ownership of a house (dar). The author explains that if someone says 'this house is for Zayd but its building is for myself,' the exception is invalid, and both the house and the building go to Zayd (the confesse). The reason is that the building is a dependent (tabi') part of the house; the name 'dar' refers to the open ground (arsa) and the building is a description within it. When one confesses to the house, the building is included by dependency, not as a primary object. Verbal exception (istithna') operates only on what is directly included under the word; since the building is not directly included (it is a description, not a part), the exception fails. However, if the exception is of a portion like 'except a third' or 'except a room,' it is valid because these are integral parts of the house. The passage then discusses a variant: if the confessor says 'the building is for me and its open ground (arsa) is for you,' the ruling follows his statement: the building remains his and the ground goes to the confesse, because 'arsa' strictly denotes the empty space, not the building. But if he uses the word 'earth' (ard) instead of 'arsa', the building follows the earth, so it goes to the confesse as well, because earth is like the house—the building is its dependent. The passage further distinguishes cases where the building is confessed to a third party (Zayd) and the earth to another (Amr): each gets what was confessed to him, because once Zayd's ownership of the building is established, the confessor cannot override it by confessing the earth to Amr. Conversely, if the confessor first confesses the earth to someone and later claims the building for himself or another, his later statement is not accepted because the building automatically follows the earth. The key principle is that the building follows the land/earth in ownership unless explicitly separated in a manner consistent with legal rules.

Key Terms
دار (dar): A house, consisting of both the open ground (arsa) and the building.
عرصة (arsa): The open ground or courtyard of a house, without building.
استثناء (istithna'): A verbal exception, excluding something from a statement.
تبعية (taba'iyya): Dependency: something that follows the primary object in ruling.
وصف (wasf): A description or attribute, as opposed to the substance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone confesses 'This house is for Zayd, but the building is for me,' what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The building goes to the confessor (the speaker) and the house to Zayd.
B) Both the house and the building go to Zayd.
C) The confession is void entirely.
D) Zayd gets the house, and the building is split equally.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the building is a dependent part of a house; therefore, excepting it in an iqrar is invalid, but excepting a definite part is valid.

Distinction Between Arsa and Ard in Iqrar
Ruling on the distinction between 'arsa' and 'ard' in iqrar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between using 'arsa' (open ground) and 'ard' (earth) when confessing to a house, and state the resulting ownership of the building.

Core Idea
If the confessor says 'the building is mine, the arsa is yours,' the building stays; if he says 'the earth is yours,' the building follows the earth.

This lesson explores a nuance in Hanafi iqrar law: the choice of words matters. When a confessor explicitly mentions the open ground (arsa) or the earth (ard), the ownership of the building changes. The commentary explains that 'arsa' excludes the building, while 'ard' includes it, leading to different outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two variants
First variant: confessor says 'building for me, arsa for you'. Second variant: confessor says 'building for me, earth for you'.
Arsa means open ground; ard means earth/land.
2
Ruling for the arsa variant
The building remains with the confessor, arsa goes to confesse, because 'arsa' strictly means the empty space without building.
3
Ruling for the ard variant
The building also goes to the confesse because the earth (ard) is like the house; the building follows it by dependency.
4
Understand the reason
The word 'ard' carries the same scope as 'dar' regarding the building; it includes the building as a dependent. 'Arsa' is narrower.
This is a linguistic distinction.
5
Apply the principle
When the confessor uses 'arsa', he effectively separates the building. When he uses 'ard', the dependency rule applies.

تبعية (taba'iyya): Dependency: something that follows the primary object in ruling.

Separate Confessions of Building and Earth to Different Persons
Ruling on separate confessions of building and earth to different persons.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between scenarios where the building and earth are confessed to different persons, and state the ownership outcome based on the order and dependency.

Core Idea
When building and earth are confessed separately to different persons, each gets their share; but if the earth is confessed first, the building follows it.

This lesson covers complex scenarios in Hanafi iqrar where the confessor assigns the building and the earth to different individuals. The ruling depends on the order of confession and the principle of dependency. Understanding these rules prevents contradictions in ownership claims.

Guided Path
1
Scenario 1: Building to Zayd, Earth to Amr simultaneously
Both confessions are valid; each gets what was confessed to him, because ownership is established at the time of confession.
There is no conflict because they are separate objects.
2
Scenario 2: Earth confessed first, then building claimed for oneself or another
The building follows the earth; the later claim is not accepted because the building already belongs to the confesse of the earth.
3
Scenario 3: Building confessed to Zayd, Earth to Amr
Each gets what is confessed to him; Zayd owns the building, Amr owns the earth.
This is the same as scenario 1 but with building first.
4
Identify the underlying principle
When the earth is confessed to someone, the building automatically becomes theirs by dependency. Subsequent statements to the contrary are ineffective because the confessor cannot take back what he has already given.
A confession is binding on the confessor.
5
Distinguish from earlier cases
In earlier cases, the confessor kept the building for himself; here he gives it to another. The dependency rule still applies.

ولو استثنى بناء دار أقر بها، كانا للمقر له؛ لأن الأستثناء لا يصح؛ لأن البناء إنما يدخل بالتبعية، وما هو كذلك لا يصح استثناؤه. [٢] قوله : ولو استثنى...الخ؛ يعني لو أقر بدار واستثنى بناءها لنفسه، بأن قال : هذه الدار لزيد، وبناؤها لنفسي، كان الدار والبناء جميعاً للمقر له؛ لأن البناء دخل في لفظ الإقرار بالدار تبعاً لا مقصوداً، فإن اسم الدار لا يتناول البناء مقصوداً؛ لأن الدار اسم للعرصة، والبناء وصف فيه، والوصف يدخل تبعاً لا قصداً، والاستثناء تصرف لفظي فما يتناوله اسم الدار لا يتحقق فيه عمل الاستثناء، فلا يصح. بخلاف ما إذا قال: إلا ثلثها، أو إلا بيتاً منها، حيث يصح الاستثناء، ويكون للمقر له ما عدا ثلث الدار، وما عدا البيت؛ لأن أجزاء الدار داخلة تحت لفظ الدار فصح استثناؤها، حتى لو استحق هذا الجزء في بيع الدار يسقط حصته من الثمن. وقوله : وعرصتها لك؛ عرصه الدار: ساحتها، وهي البقعة الواسعة التي ليس فيها بناء، والجمع عراص، مثل: كلبة وكِلاب، وعَرصات، مثل سجدة وسجدات. وقال أبو المنصور التَّعَالِبي: كل بقعة ليس فيها بناء فهي عرصة، وفي كلام ابن فارس له نحو ذلك، وفي التهذيب: سُمِّيت ساحة الدار عرصة؛ لأن الصبيان يعترصون فيها؛ أي يلعبون ويمرحون. كذا في «المصباح المنير». وقوله : فكما قال؛ يعني يكون البناء للمقر، والعرصة للمقر له؛ لأن العرصة عبارة عن البقعة دون البناء، فصار كأنه قال: بياضُ هذا الدار دون البناء لفلان، بخلاف ما إذا قال: مكان العرصة الأرض، بأن قال: بناء هذه الدار لي وأرضها لفلان، حيث يكون له البناء أيضاً؛ لأن الأرض كالدار فيتبعها البناء. بخلاف ما إذا قال بناء هذه الدار لزيد والأرض لعمرو، حيث يكون لكل واحد منهما ما أقر به له؛ لأنه لما أقر بالبناء لزيدٍ صار ملكاً له فلا يخرج من ملكه بإقراره لعمرو بالأرض، إذ لا يصدق قوله في حق غيره، بخلاف المسألة الأولى؛ لأن البناء مملولاً له، فإذا أقرّ بالأرض لغيره يتبعها؛ لأن إقراره مقبول في حق نفسه. ولو قال : أرض هذه الدار لفلان وبناؤها لي أو لفلان، كان الكل للأول؛ لأنه لما أقر بالأرض له ملك البناء تبعاً، فلا يقبل قوله بعد ذلك أنه لغيره، ولو قال : بناء هذه الدار لفلان وأرضها لفلان فلكل واحدٍ منهما ما أقر له به؛ لقيام ملكه عند الإقرار.
And if he made an exception of the building of a house which he confessed [to owning], both are for the confesse; because the exception is invalid; for the building enters only as a dependent, and what is like that, its exception is not valid. [2] His statement: 'And if he excepted...' means: if he confessed to a house and excepted its building for himself, saying: 'This house is for Zayd, and its building for myself,' both the house and the building are for the confesse; because the building entered the wording of the confession of the house as a dependent, not as an intended object. Indeed, the name 'house' does not comprehend the building as an intended object; because 'house' is a name for the open ground (arsa), and the building is a description in it, and the description enters dependently, not intentionally. Exception is a verbal operation, and what the name 'house' covers, the operation of exception is not realized in it, so it is invalid. Unlike if he said: 'except a third of it,' or 'except a room of it,' where the exception is valid, and the confesse gets what is other than a third of the house and other than the room; because the parts of the house are included under the word 'house,' so their exception is valid. So much so that if this part is claimed in the sale of the house, its portion of the price is dropped. And his statement: 'and its open ground (arsa) is for you.' 'Arsat al-dar' means its courtyard, the wide space that has no building. The plural is 'aras' like 'kalba' and 'kilab', and 'arasat' like 'sajda' and 'sajadat'. Abu al-Mansur al-Tha'alibi said: every space that has no building is an 'arsa'. In the words of Ibn Faris there is something similar. And in al-Tahdhib: the courtyard of a house is called 'arsa' because children play (ya'tarisun) there. As in al-Misbah al-Munir. And his statement: 'it is as he said' means: the building is for the confessor and the open ground is for the confesse; because 'arsa' means the space without building, so it is as if he said: 'the empty part of this house without the building is for so-and-so.' Unlike if he used the word 'earth' instead of 'arsa', saying: 'the building of this house is for me and its earth for so-and-so,' where the building is also for him (the confessor); because the earth is like the house, so the building follows it. Unlike if he said: 'the building of this house is for Zayd and the earth for Amr,' where each gets what he confessed to him; because when he confessed the building to Zayd, it became his property, so it does not leave his ownership by his confession of the earth to Amr, since his statement is not credible against others. This is different from the first issue; because the building is his property, so when he confesses the earth to someone else, it (the building) follows it; because his confession is accepted regarding himself. And if he said: 'the earth of this house is for so-and-so and its building for me or for so-and-so,' then all is for the first [mentioned]; because when he confessed the earth to him, the building becomes his as a dependent, so his subsequent statement that it is for someone else is not accepted. And if he said: 'the building of this house is for so-and-so and its earth for so-and-so,' then each gets what he confessed to him; because of the establishment of his ownership at the time of confession.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on al-Wiqayah's chapter on iqrar (confession), specifically addressing the ruling on excepting (istithna') the building (bina') when confessing to ownership of a house (dar). The author explains that if someone says 'this house is for Zayd but its building is for myself,' the exception is invalid, and both the house and the building go to Zayd (the confesse). The reason is that the building is a dependent (tabi') part of the house; the name 'dar' refers to the open ground (arsa) and the building is a description within it. When one confesses to the house, the building is included by dependency, not as a primary object. Verbal exception (istithna') operates only on what is directly included under the word; since the building is not directly included (it is a description, not a part), the exception fails. However, if the exception is of a portion like 'except a third' or 'except a room,' it is valid because these are integral parts of the house. The passage then discusses a variant: if the confessor says 'the building is for me and its open ground (arsa) is for you,' the ruling follows his statement: the building remains his and the ground goes to the confesse, because 'arsa' strictly denotes the empty space, not the building. But if he uses the word 'earth' (ard) instead of 'arsa', the building follows the earth, so it goes to the confesse as well, because earth is like the house—the building is its dependent. The passage further distinguishes cases where the building is confessed to a third party (Zayd) and the earth to another (Amr): each gets what was confessed to him, because once Zayd's ownership of the building is established, the confessor cannot override it by confessing the earth to Amr. Conversely, if the confessor first confesses the earth to someone and later claims the building for himself or another, his later statement is not accepted because the building automatically follows the earth. The key principle is that the building follows the land/earth in ownership unless explicitly separated in a manner consistent with legal rules.

Key Terms
تبعية (taba'iyya): Dependency: something that follows the primary object in ruling.
إقرار (iqrar): A legal confession or acknowledgment of a right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person says 'The earth of this house is for X' and later says 'The building of this house is for Y,' who gets the building?
A) X gets the building.
B) Y gets the building.
C) The building is split between X and Y.
D) The confessor keeps the building.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi iqrar, if the earth is confessed first, the building automatically follows; subsequent contradictory confessions are ineffective.

Exception in Confession: Subordinate Parts Cannot Be Excepted
Ruling with linguistic reasoning on exception in confession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on exception (istithna') in confessions concerning subordinates (tabi') and apply it to scenarios like building, gem, and palm tree.

Core Idea
In confession, exception of a subordinate item is invalid because it was never directly intended by the name.

When someone confesses ownership of a house but tries to exclude the building, does that exception hold? The Hanafi school says no, because the word 'house' linguistically refers to the land, and the building is only a subordinate description. This lesson unpacks the linguistic reasoning and applies it to similar cases like a ring's gem or an orchard's palm tree. Understanding this rule is crucial for correctly determining property ownership in confession-based disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is a confession (iqrar) of ownership followed by an exception (istithna). The ruling is that the exception is invalid if the excepted item is a subordinate (tabi') of the confessed property. Identify which scenarios in the passage are ruled invalid and which are valid.
Invalid: exception of building from house, gem from ring, palm tree from orchard. Valid: exception of a third or a room from a house.
2
Understand the linguistic basis
The commentator explains that the name 'house' (dar) denotes the open land (arsa), and the building (bina) is only a description that enters subsidiarily (tab'an). Exception is a verbal operation that only affects what is directly included (maqsud) in the name. Subordinates are not directly included, so the exception fails.
Contrast with a room (bayt) which is a direct part of the house, so its exception is valid.
3
Apply the rule to the 'building and land' scenario
If one says 'the building is mine and the open land is yours', the building belongs to the confessor and the land to the other. This is because the open land is the main entity and the building is subordinate. However, if he says 'land' (ard) instead of 'open land', the building goes with the land because 'land' also includes the building as a follower.
The distinction between 'arsa' (vacant land) and 'ard' (earth) affects the outcome.
4
Distinguish between confessing to oneself vs. to two different persons
If the confessor says 'the building is for Zayd and the land is for Amr', each gets what was acknowledged to him. This is because the confessor's statement is accepted regarding his own rights but not to transfer another's property. The building becomes Zayd's by confession and cannot be taken away by a later statement about the land.
This differs from the earlier case where the building was owned by the confessor himself.
5
Apply the analogy to ring's gem and orchard's palm tree
The gem of a ring and a palm tree in an orchard are like the building in a house: they are subordinates. Therefore, exception of them is invalid. However, if one declares separate ownership (e.g., 'the band is for X and the gem is for Y'), it is valid because there is no exception—rather, it is a direct confession of separate ownership.
The principle consistently relies on whether the item is included as a direct part or as a subordinate follower.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قال : بناؤها لي وعرصتها لك فكما قال
زبدة النهاية لعمدة الرعاية
لفظ الإقرار بالدار تبعاً لا مقصوداً، فإن اسم الدار لا يتناول البناء مقصوداً؛ لأن الدار اسم للعرصة، والبناء وصف فيه، والوصف يدخل تبعاً لا قصداً، والاستثناء تصرف لفظي فما يتناوله اسم الدار لا يتحقق فيه عمل الاستثناء فلا يصح. بخلاف ما إذا قال: إلا ثلثها، أو إلا بيتاً منها، حيث يصح الاستثناء، ويكون للمقر له ما عدا ثلث الدار وما عدا البيت؛ لأن أجزاء الدار داخلة تحت لفظ الدار فصح استثناؤها، حتى لو استحق هذا الجزء في بيع الدار يسقط حصته من الثمن.
قوله : وعرصتها لك؛ عرصة الدار: ساحتها، وهي البقعة الواسعة التي ليس فيها بناء، والجمع عراص مثل كلبة وكِلاب، وعرصات مثل سجدة وسجدات. وقال أبو المنصور الثعالبي : كل بقعة ليس فيها بناء فهي عرصة، وفي كلام ابن فارس نحو ذلك، وفي التهذيب: سميت ساحة الدار عرصة لأن الصبيان يعترصون فيها أي يلعبون ويمرحون. كذا في المصباح المنير.
قوله : فكما قال؛ يعني يكون البناء للمقر، والعرصة للمقر له؛ لأن العرصة عبارة عن البقعة دون البناء، فصار كأنه قال: بياض هذا الدار دون البناء لفلان، بخلاف ما إذا قال: مكان العرصة الأرض، بأن قال: بناء هذه الدار لي وأرضها لفلان، حيث يكون له البناء أيضاً؛ لأن الأرض كالدار فيتبعها البناء.
بخلاف ما إذا قال: بناء هذه الدار لزيد والأرض لعمرو، حيث يكون لكل واحد منهما ما أقر به له؛ لأنه لما أقر بالبناء لزيد صار ملكاً له فلا يخرج من ملكه بإقراره لعمرو بالأرض، إذ لا يصدق قوله في حق غيره، بخلاف المسألة الأولى؛ لأن البناء مملوك له، فإذا أقر بالأرض لغيره يتبعها؛ لأن إقراره مقبول في حق نفسه.
ولو قال: أرض هذه الدار لفلان وبناؤها لي أو لفلان، كان الكل للأول؛ لأنه لما أقر للأرض له ملك البناء تبعاً، فلا يقبل قوله بعد ذلك أنه لغيره، ولو قال: بناء هذه الدار لفلان وأرضها لفلان فلكل واحد منهما ما أقر له به؛ لقيام ملكه عند الإقرار
وفص الخاتم، ونخلة البستان كبنائها، فإن قال: هذا الخاتم لفلان إلا فصه، أو هذا البستان له إلا نخلة لا الاستثناء، ولو قال: إن الحلقة له، والفص لي، أو الأرض له، والنخل لي يصح.
قوله كبنائها؛ فكما لا يصح استثناء البناء لا يصح استثناء الفص والنخلة، وكذا طوق الجارية. كما صرح به في بعض الكتب، فإن دخول الفص في الخاتم بالتبعية، وكذا دخول النخلة في البستان، فلا يصح الاستثناء.
And if he said: its building is mine and its open land is yours, then it is as he said. Summary of the ultimate essence for the support of the guidance: The wording of the confession concerning the house is subsidiary, not intended; because the name 'house' does not include the building in an intended sense; because 'house' is the name for the open land, and the building is a description within it, and the description enters subsidiarily, not intentionally. And exception is a verbal action, so what the name 'house' encompasses, the operation of exception does not take effect in it, so it is invalid. Unlike if he said: except one third of it, or except a room of it, where the exception is valid, and the one in whose favor the confession is made gets what is beyond one third of the house and what is beyond the room; because the parts of the house are included under the word 'house', so their exception is valid, such that if this part is claimed in a sale of the house, its share of the price is reduced. His statement: 'and its open land is yours'; the open land of the house: its vacant area, which is the spacious piece of ground that has no building in it, the plural is 'urās like kalbah and kilāb, and 'araṣāt like sajdah and sajadāt. Abu al-Mansur al-Tha'alibi said: Every piece of ground that has no building in it is an 'arṣah. In the words of Ibn Faris is something similar. And in al-Tahdhib: The courtyard of the house was called 'arṣah because children play and sport in it. This is in al-Misbah al-Munir. His statement: 'then it is as he said'; meaning the building belongs to the confessor, and the open land to the one in whose favor the confession is made; because the 'arṣah is the piece without the building, so it is as if he said: the vacant space of this house without the building is for so-and-so. Unlike if he said instead of 'open land' 'land', by saying: the building of this house is mine and its land is for so-and-so, where the building also goes to him; because the land is like the house, so the building follows it. Unlike if he said: the building of this house is for Zayd and the land is for 'Amr, where each of them has what he acknowledged for him; because when he acknowledged the building for Zayd, it became his property, so it does not leave his property by his acknowledgment for 'Amr of the land, since his statement is not believed concerning another. Unlike the first issue; because the building is owned by him, so when he acknowledges the land for another, it follows it; because his acknowledgment is accepted concerning himself. And if he said: the land of this house is for so-and-so and its building is for me or for so-and-so, everything is for the first; because when he acknowledged the land for him, he owned the building as a follower, so his statement afterward that it is for another is not accepted. And if he said: the building of this house is for so-and-so and its land is for so-and-so, then each of them has what he acknowledged for him; because his ownership was established at the time of the acknowledgment. And the gem of the ring and the palm tree of the orchard are like its building. If he said: this ring is for so-and-so except its gem, or this orchard is for him except a palm tree, the exception is invalid. And if he said: the band is for him and the gem is for me, or the land is for him and the palm trees are for me, it is valid. His statement: 'like its building'; for just as the exception of the building is invalid, so too the exception of the gem and the palm tree, and likewise the collar of the slave girl, as clarified in some books. Because the gem enters the ring as a follower, and likewise the palm tree enters the orchard, so the exception is invalid.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on a ruling from the matn concerning exception (istithnā') in confessions (iqrār). The central issue: when a person confesses ownership of a house (dār) but then makes an exception for the building (binā'). The commentator explains that the term 'house' linguistically refers to the land (ʿarṣah), and the building is included only as a subordinate (tabʿan), not as an independent object. Therefore, attempting to except the building is invalid because exception is a verbal operation that only works on what is directly included in the name. Similarly, if one says 'the building is mine and the land is yours', the building belongs to the confessor and the land to the other, since the land is the main entity. The commentator then distinguishes cases where the land is called 'arḍ (earth), where the building follows the land. Further, he explains the difference when two different persons are named: if the building is acknowledged for one and the land for another, each keeps what was acknowledged for him, because the confessor's statement is accepted regarding himself but not others. The same principle applies to a ring's gem (faṣṣ) and an orchard's palm tree (nakhlah): they are subordinate to the main item, so exception is invalid. However, if the components are declared as separate ownerships (e.g., the band for one and the gem for another), it is valid.

Key Terms
عرصة (ʿarṣah): The open land of a house, the vacant area without building.
تبعاً (tabʿan): Subsidiarily or as a follower; the building is included under the name 'house' only as a subordinate.
استثناء (istithnāʾ): Exception, a verbal act of excluding part of what is included in a general statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone says, 'I confess this ring is for Zaid except its gem,' is the exception valid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Yes, because the gem is part of the ring.
B) No, because the gem is a subordinate and not directly intended by the word 'ring'.
C) Yes, because an exception can exclude any specific item.
D) No, because the ring already belongs to Zaid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the validity of an exception in a confession depends on whether the excepted item is directly intended by the name of the confessed property; subordinates cannot be excepted.

Confession of Debt from Price of a Slave: Conditions and Cases
Ruling on conditional confession of debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a confession that is tied to a specific countervalue (thaman ʿabd) and distinguish the three sub-cases where the debt becomes binding or not.

Core Idea
A debt confessed on a specific condition is binding only when that condition is fulfilled.

In this passage, the commentator explains a nuanced area of iqrar (confession). A person confesses a debt of one thousand dirhams but ties it to the price of a slave he bought yet never received. The ruling depends on whether the slave is delivered and on the parties' agreement about the transaction. We will unpack the main rule and its three variations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the confessor's statement and the condition
Read the opening sentence: the confessor says 'I owe a thousand from the price of a slave I bought from you and did not take possession.' Note the condition: it is a debt specifically from the price of a slave (thaman ʿabd).
The confession is conditional (ʿalā ṣifah).
2
Understand the main ruling
If the confessor specifies the slave, the claimant confirms, and the claimant delivers the slave, then the debt is binding on the confessor. If the slave is not delivered, the debt is not binding by consensus.
The debt is tied to the countervalue; without delivery, no obligation.
3
Analyze the three sub-cases
Case 1: Claimant confirms and delivers the specified slave → debt binding. Case 2: Claimant says 'this is your slave, I sold you another' → still binding because they agree on entitlement, differing only on cause. Case 3: Claimant says 'this is my slave, I did not sell it' → no debt binding.
The key is agreement on entitlement vs denial of sale.
4
Apply the rationale: confession on a description
The confession is only binding as per the description (ṣifah) stated. Since the debt was conditioned on the slave delivery, it does not become due without that condition.
Hanafi law enforces confessions according to the confessor's own conditions.
5
Examine the analogy with usurpation vs loan
The commentator compares case 2 to someone confessing usurpation of 1000 dirhams, and the claimant says it was a loan. They disagree on cause but agree on entitlement; payment is ordered.
Qiyas: when the objective (payment of debt) is achieved, the cause dispute becomes irrelevant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال : له على ألف من ثمن عبد اشتريته منه ولم أقبضه، فإن عينه بأن ذكر عبداً بعينه وصدقه المقر له في شرائه وعدم قبضه، قيل للمقر له : سلم العبد إلى المقر، وخذ ثمنه منه، فإن سلم المقر له ذلك العبد المعين بأن يحضره بين يديه، لزم الألف على المقر بهذا القيد؛ لأنه أقر له بألف على صفة، فيلزمه على الصفة التي أقر بها، وإن لم يسلم العبد إلى المقر لا يلزمه الألف إجماعاً، وهذه المسألة على وجوه: أحدها: ما ذكره المصنف، وهو ما إذا صدقه وسلمه إليه، وحكمه ما تقدم من لزوم الألف على المقر بالقيد المذكور؛ لأن ما ثبت بتصادقهما يكون كالثابت عياناً. والثاني: أن يقول المقر له: إن هذا العبد عبدك ما بعتكه، وإنما بعتك عبداً آخر، وسلمته إليك، والحكم فيه كالأول؛ لأنهما اتفقا على ما أقر به من أن كل واحد منهما يستحق ما أقر به، غير أنهما اختلفا في سبب الاستحقاق، ولا يبالي باختلافها، ولا باختلاف السبب عند حصول المقصود واتحاد الحكم، فصار كما إذا أقر له بغصب ألف درهم، فقال المقر له: هي قرض، فإنه يؤمر بالدفع إليه لاتفاقهما على الاستحقاق. والثالث: أن يقول المقر له: إن هذا العبد عبدي ما بعتكه، وحكمه أن لا يلزم على المقر شيء؛ لأنه لم يقر بالمال إلا عوضاً عن العبد، فلا يلزمه دونه.
If he said: He owes me one thousand from the price of a slave whom I bought from him and did not take possession, then if he specified it by mentioning a particular slave and the one in whose favor the confession is made confirmed him in the purchase and non-possession, it is said to the one in whose favor the confession is made: Deliver the slave to the confessor and take its price from him. If the one in whose favor the confession is made delivers that specified slave by bringing it before him, the thousand is binding upon the confessor with this condition; because he confessed a thousand on a description, so it is binding upon him according to the description with which he confessed. And if he does not deliver the slave to the confessor, the thousand is not binding upon him by consensus. This issue has aspects: one is what the author mentioned, which is when he confirms and delivers it to him, its ruling is what preceded: the binding of the thousand upon the confessor with the mentioned condition; because what is established by their mutual confirmation is like established by eyewitness. The second: that the one in whose favor the confession is made says: This slave is your slave, I did not sell it to you, but I sold you another slave and delivered it to you. Its ruling is like the first; because they agreed on what he confessed: that each of them deserves what he confessed, except they differed on the cause of deserving, and their difference is not considered, nor the difference of cause, when the objective is achieved and the ruling is unified. So it is like when he confessed he owed a thousand dirhams by usurpation, and the one in whose favor it is said: it is a loan; then he is ordered to pay it to him because of their agreement on the entitlement. The third: that the one in whose favor the confession is made says: This slave is my slave, I did not sell it to you. Its ruling is that nothing is binding upon the confessor; because he only confessed the wealth as a substitute for the slave, so it is not binding without it.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where a person confesses a debt of one thousand dirhams specifically from the price of a slave (thaman ʿabd) that he bought but did not take possession of. The commentator explains the ruling from the matn: if the confessor specifies the slave, and the claimant confirms the sale and non-delivery, then the claimant must hand over the slave to receive payment. The debt becomes binding only upon delivery of the specified slave. If the slave is not delivered, the debt is not binding by consensus. Three sub-cases are examined: (1) Both agree on the slave and delivery occurs – the debt is binding. (2) The claimant says the slave is the confessor's and he sold a different slave – this is treated the same as case (1) because they agree on entitlement, even if the cause differs; analogous to a case of usurpation versus loan. (3) The claimant denies the sale entirely and claims the slave as his own – then no debt is binding because the confessor only promised the price in exchange for the slave.

Key Terms
ثمن عبد (thaman ʿabd): The price (purchase money) of a slave. Here, the debt is specifically from that price.
على صفة (ʿalā ṣifah): With a description; the confessor specified the debt as 'from the price of a slave', so it is binding only if that description is fulfilled.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a person confesses a debt of one thousand dirhams from the price of a slave bought but not delivered, what happens if the claimant denies the sale and says the slave is his own?
A) The confessor must pay the thousand dirhams.
B) The confessor must pay only if he acknowledges the slave is the claimant's.
C) Nothing is binding on the confessor because the debt was conditional on the slave exchange.
D) The claimant must prove the sale for the debt to be binding.

Key Takeaway
A conditional confession (iqrar muqayyad) is enforced only as per the condition; the debt is not due until the specified countervalue is delivered.

Ruling on 'Mā Qabaḍtuhu' with Specification
Ruling on muqir's statement about a specific slave and its effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muqir's acknowledgment qualified by 'ma qabadtuhu' and identify when the debt becomes binding based on specification and delivery.

Core Idea
A muqir's claim of non-receipt only protects liability if he specifies the exact item and the creditor fails to deliver.

In Hanafi law, an acknowledgment (iqrar) is generally binding unless the muqir qualifies it with a condition. The phrase 'ma qabadtuhu' (what I have not received) attached to a specific item can suspend liability. This lesson examines the condition of specification and delivery from the source text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and qualification
The muqir acknowledges a debt and adds 'ma qabadtuhu' referring to a specific item (e.g., a slave). Distinguish between specifying the item and not specifying.
The phrase 'ma qabadtuhu' is a description of the item.
2
Distinguish specified vs. unspecified
If the muqir specifies the item (e.g., 'this slave'), the debt is conditional; if unspecified, the debt is binding immediately and the phrase is void.
Specification is key to the exception.
3
Determine the condition for binding
When specified, the debt becomes binding only if the muqarr lahu (creditor) delivers the specified item to the muqir.
Delivery is a condition for liability.
4
Understand the legal effect of 'ma qabadtuhu'
The phrase does not automatically negate liability; it creates a condition that suspends binding effect until delivery.
Without specification, it has no effect.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a case where the muqir specifies a slave and the creditor does not deliver, the debt is not binding.
Contrast with the case without specification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما قبضته، وعينه ، فإن سَلّمَهُ المُقَر له لَزِمَهُ الألف وإلا لا، وإن لم يعين لَزِمَه ، وما قبضته لغو. ما قبضته، وعينه ، فإن سَلّمَهُ المُقَر له لَزِمَهُ الألفُ والا لا)، قوله : ما قبضته : صفة العبد، وقوله : وعينه : أي عين العبد، وهو في يدِ المُقَرِّ له ، فَإِنَّ سلّمَ الْمُقَوله ذلك إلى المُقِرِّ لَزِمَهُ الألف وإلا لا.
What I have received, and he specified it, then if the one acknowledged for him delivers it, the thousand becomes binding, otherwise not; and if he did not specify, it is binding upon him, and what I have received is void. 'What I have received': description of the slave, and 'specified it': i.e., he specified the slave, and it is in the hand of the one acknowledged for him. So if the one acknowledged for him delivers that to the muqir, the thousand becomes binding, otherwise not.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
The passage states a ruling: when someone acknowledges a debt of one thousand dirhams and then says it is from the price of a specific slave that he has not received (ma qabadtuhu), if he specifies that slave and the muqarr lahu (creditor) actually delivers that slave to the muqir, then the thousand becomes binding. If the creditor does not deliver, the debt is not binding. The key is that the item is specified ('ayyanahu) and in the creditor's hand. The commentary clarifies that 'ma qabadtuhu' is an attribute of the slave, and 'specified it' means he identified the particular slave.

Key Terms
ما قبضته (mā qabaḍtuhu): A statement by the muqir meaning 'what I have not received', referring to the item whose price is being acknowledged.
عينه (‘ayyanahu): The muqir specified the exact item (e.g., a particular slave) that the debt is from.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a muqir says 'I owe 1000 dirhams from the price of this slave, which I have not received,' when does the 1000 become binding?
A) Immediately upon the acknowledgment.
B) Only if the muqir specifies the slave and the muqarr lahu delivers it.
C) Only if the muqir does not specify the slave.
D) It is never binding.

Key Takeaway
The debt becomes binding only if the muqir specifies the item and the creditor delivers it.

Unspecific Acknowledgment and the Effect of Denial of Receipt
Ruling on unspecific acknowledgment with denial of receipt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a denial of receipt (ma qabadtuhu) is ineffective when the acknowledgment is unspecified, and state the ruling that the acknowledgment remains binding.

Core Idea
An unspecified item is like destroyed goods; denying receipt of it is a void retraction, not a valid exception.

Imagine a debtor admits owing 1000 dirhams but adds 'I did not receive the goods.' Does this denial help him? This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains that if the goods are unspecified, the acknowledgment is binding and the denial is void. The reasoning is based on the Hanafi principle that an unspecified item is legally equivalent to a destroyed item, making delivery impossible and thus the price not obligatory. Let's analyze the ruling and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The muqir makes an unspecific acknowledgment (e.g., 'I owe 1000 for a slave I have not received'). The ruling: the debt is binding, and the exception (denial of receipt) is void (laghw).
2
Understand the Legal Fiction
Jahl al-mabigh (ignorance of the sold item) is treated as destruction because delivery is impossible. The buyer can reject any specific item presented, so the item is legally like destroyed.
This is a Hanafi principle: jahalah fatal in contracts.
3
Trace the Consequence
Since the item is like destroyed, the price was never obligatory upon the muqir until receipt. Therefore, his denial of receipt is actually a retraction of the acknowledgment, which is invalid.
The denial directly negates the basis of the obligation.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa holds the denial is void even if said immediately (muttasil). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold it is valid if said immediately. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) view is Abu Hanifa's.
The ikhtilaf is on the condition of connectivity; but for unspecified, the denial is always void per the preferred view.
5
Apply in Practice
In court, a debtor's statement 'I owe for an unspecified item but haven't received it' is ineffective. The debt is binding, and the denial does not help.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن لم يعين لَزِمَه ، وما قبضته لغو. قوله : لأن إنكار القبض في غير المعين ينافي الوجوب أصلاً ؛ لأن جهالة المبيع في حكم هلاكه ؛ لعدم القدرة على تسليم المجهول، فيمتنع وجوب نقد الثمن، وإذا كان كذلك كان رجوعاً فلا يصح وإن كان موصولاً. قوله : ينافي الوجوب؛ لأنَّ ثمن عبد غير معين لا يكون واجباً على المشتري إلا بعد القبض؛ لأنَّ ما لا يكون بعينه فهو في حكم المستهلك؛ لأنه لا طريق للوصول إليه، فإنّه ما من عبد يحضره إلا وللمشتري أن يقول المبيع غير هذا، وتسليم الثمن لا يجب إلا بإحضار المبيع، فعلم أنه في حكم المستهلك، فكأنه أقر بالقبض ثم رجع.
And if he did not specify, it is binding upon him, and 'what I have received' is void. (Commentary:) Because denial of receipt in an unspecified matter entirely negates obligation; because the ignorance of the sold item is like its destruction, due to inability to deliver the unknown, so the obligation to pay the price is prevented, and when that is the case, it is a retraction and thus invalid even if connected. (Another commentary:) It negates obligation because the price of an unspecified slave is not obligatory upon the buyer except after receipt; because what is not specified is like consumed goods, since there is no way to reach it; indeed, no slave he brings forth except that the buyer can say 'the sold item is not this', and payment of the price is not obligatory except upon producing the sold item, so it is known that it is like consumed goods, as if he acknowledged receipt and then retracted.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling when the muqir does not specify the item (e.g., says 'I owe 1000 dirhams from the price of a slave I have not received' without identifying the slave). In that case, according to Abu Hanifa, the debt is binding, and the statement 'ma qabadtuhu' is void (لغو). The reason given is that denying receipt for an unspecified item is actually a retraction of the acknowledgment, because an unspecified item is legally like a destroyed item (halak) — since it is impossible to deliver an unknown thing. Therefore, the price cannot be obligatory in the first place, so the statement is a retraction and invalid even if said immediately (muttasil). The commentary elaborates: the price of an unspecified slave is not payable until receipt because the buyer can always claim any presented slave is not the one intended; thus it is like the goods are consumed, and the muqir's denial is equivalent to taking back his admission.

Key Terms
لغو (laghw): Here meaning 'void' or 'ineffective'; the statement does not affect the obligation.
جهالة المبيع (jahālat al-mabī‘): Ignorance or uncertainty regarding the sold item; legally treated as destruction because delivery is impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the denial of receipt in an unspecified item considered a retraction?
A) Because the muqir is lying.
B) Because the item is like consumed goods and cannot be delivered, so the price was never obligatory.
C) Because the muqir forgot the item.
D) Because the creditor did not sue.

Key Takeaway
An unspecific acknowledgment with denial of receipt is binding; the denial is void because the unspecified item is legally like a destroyed item, preventing the obligation from arising.

Connectivity of Exception in Acknowledgment: Sahibayn's View
Intra-Hanafi dispute on effect of connected exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on the effect of a connected exception in an acknowledgment, and distinguish it from Abu Hanifa's position.

Core Idea
A connected exception in acknowledgment is accepted as an explanatory change if it clarifies the basis of the debt.

This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) on the validity of an exception in acknowledgment. The Sahibayn allow a connected exception that changes the implication of the first statement, while Abu Hanifa rejects it outright as a retraction. Understanding this distinction clarifies when a muqir's subsequent clarification is accepted as an elaboration rather than a retraction.

Guided Path
1
Locate the disagreement
Identify the differing positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on a muqir's exception regarding an unspecified item (e.g., 'except that I never received the slave'). Abu Hanifa considers such an exception a retraction and invalid; Sahibayn consider it a permissible explanatory change if connected.
The source passage focuses on Sahibayn's view, but the dispute is with Abu Hanifa.
2
Understand Sahibayn's ruling on connectivity
According to Sahibayn, if the exception is connected (muttasil) to the acknowledgment, the muqir is believed. If disconnected (munfasil), he is believed only if the muqarr lahu (creditor) confirms the reason for the exception.
Connectivity means the exception is uttered without a break immediately after the acknowledgment.
3
Analyze the reasoning (talil)
The muqir's explanation is a 'bayān taghyīr' (explanatory change) that modifies the implication of immediate payment to deferred payment until receipt of the item. This change is valid when connected because it does not retract the acknowledgment but clarifies its basis.
The source passage states: 'he acknowledged an obligation of money and gave a reason for it'.
4
Trace the condition of creditor confirmation
If the muqarr lahu confirms the reason (e.g., that the debt is from the price of a slave), the muqir is believed whether the exception is connected or disconnected. If the muqarr lahu denies the reason, the muqir is only believed if the exception is connected.
When the reason is confirmed by both, it is established by mutual agreement (tasāduq).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Sahibayn, a muqir can successfully use a connected exception to avoid immediate payment. Under Abu Hanifa, such an exception is always rejected, so the muqir remains liable immediately.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's view, as noted in the commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعندهما : إن وَصَلَ صُدِّق؛ لأنَّه بيان تغيير عندهما، كقوله: من ثَمَن. حاصل مذهبهما: إنّه إن صدقه المُقَرُّ له في أنّ ذلك من ثمن عبد يصدق وصل أو فصل، وإن كذَّبه في ذلك لم يصدق إلا إذا كان موصولاً، ووجه ذلك: إنّه أقر بوجوب المال، وبيَّن له سبباً، فإذا صدقه المقر له في ذلك السبب ثبت السبب بتصادقهما. ثمَّ المالُ بهذا السبب يكون واجباً قبل القبض، ولكن إنما يتأكد بالقبض، والمقر ينكر، فجعلنا القول قوله في إنكاره القبض، وإن كذبه في السبب كان هذا من المقر بياناً مغيراً لمقتضى أول الكلام؛ لأنَّ مقتضى أوّل كلامه أن يكون مطالباً بالمال للحال، ولكن احتمل أن لا يكون مطالباً به حتى يحضر العبد، وبيان التغير يصح موصولاً، ولا يصح مفصولا.
And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): if he connects (the exception), he is believed, because in their view it is an explanatory change, like saying 'from a price.' The gist of their madhhab: if the muqarr lahu confirms that it is from the price of a slave, he is believed whether connected or disconnected; but if he denies it, he is not believed unless it is connected. The reasoning: he acknowledged an obligation of money and gave a reason for it; if the muqarr lahu confirms that reason, the reason is established by their mutual confirmation. Then the money by this reason is obligatory before receipt, but it is only confirmed by receipt, and the muqir denies receipt, so we make his statement (the denial) credible. If the muqarr lahu denies the reason, then this is from the muqir a change in the meaning of the first part of his speech, because the first part implies immediate payment, but the exception implies it is not due until the slave is produced; such explanatory change is valid when connected, not when disconnected.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage presents the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (Sahibayn) in contrast to Abu Hanifa. They differentiate based on whether the exception is connected (muttasil) or disconnected (munfasil), and also on whether the muqarr lahu confirms the reason. If the creditor confirms that the debt is from the price of a slave, then the muqir's statement is believed whether connected or disconnected, because the reason is established by mutual agreement. However, if the creditor denies the reason, the muqir's explanation is only accepted if it is connected to the acknowledgment, because then it is merely an elaboration of the original statement rather than a retraction. The reasoning is that the initial acknowledgment implies immediate obligation, but the exception indicates the obligation is deferred until receipt of the slave; this is a change that can only be made immediately. The commentary criticizes the original sharh for being abbreviated and potentially misleading.

Key Terms
موصول (mawṣūl): Connected; the exception is uttered immediately after the acknowledgment without a break.
بيان تغيير (bayān taghyīr): An explanatory change that modifies the initial statement without retracting it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, when is a muqir's statement that the debt is from the price of an unspecified slave accepted?
A) Only if the muqarr lahu confirms the reason.
B) Always, whether connected or disconnected.
C) Only if the muqir is truthful.
D) Never.

Key Takeaway
The Sahibayn accept a connected exception in acknowledgment as a valid explanatory change, while Abu Hanifa rejects it as a retraction; connectivity and creditor confirmation are key conditions.
